Flour Market is Currently Good, Future is Flat 129

Yesterday, the flour market showed a trend of being firm in the near months and flat in the distant months. Due to the limited storage capacity of the factory in the current month, the sporadic sales venues are still continuing. (It is said that the price of spot flour in Tianjin has opened to 4 yuan and 5 fen.) If this route can be installed in the future, then the sales can be expected to be active. Therefore, the market sentiment is very strong, and speculators are scrambling to cover their positions. Although the quotation for foreign wheat has risen by 2 to 3 jiao in the distant months, most people believe that the foreign wheat market is still oversupplied, or foreign wheat may come to China. Therefore, the market sentiment has not been boosted, and buyers are very quiet. As a result, the prices for the current and next months have risen by 3 fen compared to the previous day. The prices for September and November have risen by 5 li, the price for October has risen by 2.5 li, and the price for December has not changed.

Wheat Market Falls and Rises Again 130

Yesterday, the wheat futures market generally showed a spiral pattern. Initially, because the inland gangs were about to enter the market for early rice, both near-term and distant-term prices were going down step by step, so the market once showed weakness. (It is said that the price of Suzhou special high wheat opened at 9 yuan, 3 jiao, and a half, which is already cheaper by 1 or 2 jiao compared to the previous price.) Later, due to the large-scale purchases by local merchants and hoarders, the market turned upward again. If the sales of flour become active, the wheat market should temporarily look promising. As a result, the prices for the current month to November remained unchanged, and the price for December was better by 1 fen. The prices of existing wheat, such as Shandong Chen Bai Wheat, Huang Qiao, Bianjiang, and Yaowan Wheat, were similar to the previous day because the factories rarely showed interest in purchasing and the merchants were unwilling to cut prices cheaply, so the transactions were very quiet. The entire market only did more than 2,000 bales.

Silk and Tea: Shanghai Silk Factories Plan to Suspend Work During the Summer Vacation

Every year, during the hot summer months, the silk factories in this port usually reduce working hours to half-time or three-quarters (i.e., one-third) to allow for rest. Recently, overseas silk weaving factories have been trying to reduce costs due to economic reasons, mixing in rayon, which has greatly reduced the demand for raw silk. In addition, the price of Japanese silk has been falling, and the price of Chinese silk is relatively high due to high costs, so European and American silk merchants have no appetite for it. The slump in silk sales has reached an extreme point. The silk factories are now planning to suspend work temporarily during the period of reduced working hours during the summer vacation in order to save expenses.

Qining Fragrant Tea is Launched for Sale in England 131

Their interest has become more active. Yesterday, Tianyu Foreign Company in the market took the lead in purchasing more than 5,000 boxes. Other companies are also starting to take action, and the market is quite lively. The trading of green tea such as needle eyebrow and beautiful eyebrow is still not lonely. However, the very important Zhenmei tea is still being raised up and down. There is not much transaction for Qining black tea, and the market situation is still difficult to be considered optimistic.

Yesterday's Hurricane Has Passed 134

But There is a New Hurricane

May Visit a Second Time

The various circumstances of the hurricane that passed through this port the day before yesterday have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the wind force had decreased yesterday, and the weather turned sunny in the afternoon. However, the customs flagpole at Lujiazui in Pudong received a report from the observatory stating that the hurricane had already passed through Zhenjiang to the north of the Yangtze River, traveling north along the 120th meridian and reaching the 33rd parallel, causing havoc in the Jiangbei inland area. There was no danger to this port or the sea surface. Therefore, at approximately 9:00 a.m. yesterday, the black warning ball that had been hoisted was lowered. Consequently, the ocean liners that had been suspended for a day had also successively departed and exited yesterday. However, at 4:00 p.m., the Yangjingbang Observatory received a report from the Xujiahui headquarters stating that another hurricane had occurred in the east of the northern Philippine Islands in the Pacific Ocean, heading west-northward across the ocean. If it does not change direction, it will land in Fujian after passing south of Taiwan. However, the wind direction is uncertain. If it turns into a true northwest wind over the Taiwan Strait, then this port will have a second hurricane visiting it within a few days.

There are No True Cholera Bacteria in This Port 135

Announced by the Temporary Prevention and Treatment Office

The Shanghai Temporary Prevention and Treatment Office for Cholera, established in Shanghai by the Ministry of Health of the National Government, received a bulletin from the Eastern Health Bureau on the 10th of this month stating that 81 cases of cholera had occurred in Calcutta, India, with 53 deaths; 7 cases in Saigon, with 4 deaths; and 99 cases in Cebu Island, Philippines, with 50 deaths. The epidemic is spreading widely in other parts of the Philippines as well. The health authorities of this port and other ports in China are now quite worried about the spread of the epidemic in the Philippines. However, as far as Shanghai is concerned, bacteriological tests have been conducted repeatedly by Chinese and Concession health officials, and no true cholera bacteria have been found to date.

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce Orders the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Encourage the Purchase and Use of Domestically Produced Matches 136

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce instructed the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce as follows: "In order to issue an order, we have investigated that matches are a daily necessity, and the annual consumption is enormous. This business has always been controlled by foreign merchants. In recent years, domestic manufacturers have established factories and are determined to operate. Sales have gradually expanded, and the effect of saving leakage has been considerable. Recently, various parties have listed the situations of foreign merchants' aggression and monopoly, and have requested that measures be taken to provide relief, and that all institutions and groups in the country should uniformly purchase and use domestically produced matches in order to slightly reduce the trend of foreign match aggression. The Ministry has checked the various sections reported and found that they are true. In addition to studying fundamental relief policies to protect them, the request to widely encourage the purchase and use of domestic matches is indeed an essential plan. We hope that our people will understand this and encourage each other to maintain the dying match industry of this country. The order is hereby given to the Chamber to immediately comply with and devise means to encourage purchase and use, and to report the handling situation to the Supervisory Office at any time." It is heard that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has prepared a letter to inform the various trade associations to inform their affiliated businesses to uniformly purchase and use domestic matches after receiving this order.

Record of Sino-Egyptian Tariff Negotiations 138

According to foreign sources, Egypt has implemented tariff autonomy and announced new tariff regulations this year, to be effective in February. The tariff regulations are divided into maximum and minimum rates. Countries that have signed agreements with Egypt recognizing the new tariffs will be subject to the minimum rate; otherwise, the maximum rate will apply. There is no commercial treaty between China and Egypt, but Chinese tobacco exports to Egypt are substantial. Therefore, Egyptian tobacco merchants requested that China recognize the new Egyptian tariffs to reduce the tax rate. The Chinese Legation in London followed this approach, negotiating with Egypt using an "exchange of notes" format, with both parties exchanging official documents to apply the lower tax rate on the principle of reciprocity. This arrangement is limited to a one-year term and will then expire. A formal commercial treaty has not yet been signed.

Baoshan Finance Bureau Begins Collecting Taxes Busily 142

Bei Jietai, Director of the Baoshan County Finance Bureau, regarding the collection of land taxes for the 19th year of the Republic, previously requested an additional local fee of eight cents per mu of land. After approval, the order was issued to the record-keepers of each district to verify and allocate the tax silver according to the regulations, and then to calculate the equivalent amount in silver dollars. They worked overnight to create tax collection registers and send them to each counter to prepare the receipts. The procedures for starting collection have now been completed, and tax collection counters were opened yesterday. A notice was issued to all property owners in each district, requiring them to seal their payments and submit them to the counters within the deadline, paying the full amount. Furthermore, Baoshan land tax receipts have been thoroughly improved since last year. In addition to the originally allocated tax silver amount, the equivalent amount in silver dollars is added. All amounts payable by each property owner are clearly printed on the receipt, making it clear at a glance, eliminating the effort of conversion and avoiding malpractices such as surcharges. The fact that the land tax receipts include the actual amount in silver dollars was first initiated by the county finance bureau. Since the trial implementation, the results have been excellent, and the public feels very convenient.

Municipal Party Department Holds Memorial Service for Fan and Guo Yesterday 143

Fan Zhengluo and Guo Qingzhao, two martyrs, had been vigorously engaged in suppressing the communists during their lifetimes, which led to the communists' hatred. They were assassinated by the communists one after the other. The Municipal Party Department, considering that the two comrades, Fan and Guo, died for the Party and the country, specifically held a memorial service at the Penglai Grand Theatre at 9:00 AM yesterday to express their grief. Many wreaths and elegiac couplets were sent from various parties. From the central government, there were Chen Guofu, Chen Lifu, Yu Jingtang, Zhang Lisheng, Lou Tongsun, etc. From the city, there were Mayor Zhang, various bureaus of the municipal government, various departments and offices of the municipal party department, and individuals such as Tang Demin, Huang Jinrong, Cheng Ziqing, and various committees of the municipal party department. Due to the limited space in the hall, only one-third of them were displayed. The details of the meeting are described below:

A Glimpse of the Memorial Hall A high platform was set up outside the hall, and the Party and National Flag and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen were hung on the stage inside the hall. Below was a sacrificial table for the two martyrs, Fan and Guo, with portraits of the two martyrs placed on the table, covered with a white arch. Fruits, incense, and flowers were placed in the front, with wreaths on the sides. The four walls under the stage were full of elegiac banners and couplets.

Attendance In addition to Chen Junyi, Wu Kaixian, Chen Dezheng, Tong Xingbai, and Hou Dachun, members of the Municipal Party Department, and various staff members, there were also Chen Kecheng, a representative of the Municipal Government, Guo Chengxi, a representative of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, representatives from various trade unions, party departments at all levels, and other groups, totaling more than 500 people.

Meeting Order: 1. Opening of the meeting; 2. Playing of mourning music; 3. Singing of the Party song; 4. Paying the highest respects to the Party and National Flag, the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, and the portraits of Fan and Guo; 5. Chairman respectfully reading Sun Yat-sen's Last Will and Testament (Tong Xingbai); 6. Silent tribute to Fan and Guo; 7. Reading of the memorial text (Tong Xingbai); 8. Offering wreaths (Wu Hewei); 9. Chairman's report (Chen Dezheng); 10. Speeches; 11. Response from Fan's family; 12. Response from Guo's family; 13. Shouting slogans; 14. Playing mourning music; 15. Photograph; 16. Adjournment.

Family Thanks Fan Zhengluo's family was originally to be thanked by his brother, Fan Zhengbo. However, Zhengbo was so saddened by his brother's unfulfilled aspirations and the fact that he had been in danger that he was overcome with grief. Therefore, Comrade Jia Yusong represented him. Guo Qingchang represented Guo's family in giving thanks.

Memorial Text: On this 15th day of July in the 19th year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee, Supervisory Committee, and all Party members respectfully offer a sacrifice of clear wine and fragrant flowers before the spirits of Comrades Fan Zhengluo and Guo Qingzhao, saying: Alas, who can escape death? Death is sometimes heavier than Mount Tai, and sometimes lighter than a feather. Rather than following popular opinions and living to an old age, how can one compare to sacrificing oneself for the Party and the country, taking righteousness and achieving benevolence? This is the difference between a feather and Mount Tai, and this is why the deaths of the two comrades are admired and mourned by us without end. One, newly married and setting out on a long journey, did not let the feelings of family hold back the ambitions of a hero. After arriving in Shanghai for several months, he did not spare any effort to eliminate evil and punish violence. Who would have known that he would be hated by the communists and suddenly be assassinated, sacrificing himself for the sake of righteousness? That was Comrade Fan. The other, when communist heresies were rampant and ignorant workers were sometimes deceived, to prevent future troubles, especially engaged in rectifying and eliminating the red scourge, making outstanding achievements. Who would have known that he would also suddenly be assassinated, painfully becoming crippled, giving up his life for righteousness? That was Comrade Guo. Alas, the two comrades have passed away. Colleagues, who are left behind, vow to continue the fearless spirit of the two comrades, to eliminate the rebels, defend the Party and the country, realize the ideology, and save the people from fire and water, completing the unfinished aspirations of the two comrades. This is why today's memorial service is filled with weeping and sorrow, and why we use it to encourage ourselves. If the spirits of the two comrades are conscious, may they accept this humble sincerity and smile in the afterlife. Alas, may you enjoy the sacrifice.

Slogans (1) Continue the revolutionary spirit of the two martyrs; (2) The two martyrs sacrificed for the Party; (3) The two martyrs died for us; (4) The deaths of the two martyrs are a loss to our Party; (5) Vow to avenge the two martyrs; (6) Eliminate the Chinese Communist Party; (7) Complete the unfinished aspirations of the two martyrs; (8) The spirit of the two martyrs will never die; (9) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang; (10) Long live the Republic of China.

Ecuadorian Overseas Chinese Support Honorary Consul, Inquiry Yesterday 147

The Chinese Kuomintang branch in Guayaquil, Ecuador, South America, filed a case accusing Chen Xintang, Honorary Consul in the country, of 13 charges. The Ecuadorian Chinese Chamber of Commerce, considering that Consul Chen has always been admired by overseas Chinese merchants, sent a telegram to clarify the situation and express support. Details were published in this newspaper on the 14th. It has now been learned that the Overseas Chinese Promotion Association at 17 Chuanchang Road, Zhabei (moved from 478 North Sichuan Road in early June) received an express mail telegram from Gu Yuwen, President of the Chamber of Commerce, and Chen Shaozhi, Vice President (also a representative of the association in Guayaquil), requesting assistance in appealing to dispel the false accusations and seek the welfare of the overseas Chinese. The association approved this and immediately forwarded it to Hu Hanmin, a member of the Central Party Department in Nanjing, for referral to the Standing Committee and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee for investigation. An annotation was added: "We have always known that if your committee members find any mistakes in comrades after investigation, they will often offer frank advice and guidance, hoping for correction. This kind of frank spirit is admirable. Moreover, your committee members have been abroad for many years and are very familiar with the situation of overseas Chinese and party affairs. Regarding the above-mentioned incident, we believe that you will have appropriate solutions. Our association does not seem to have to worry too much. However, we would like to ask for a reply on how to handle it, so that we can pass it on to the future. We are looking forward to it."

The association also received an original document from the Ecuadorian Chinese Chamber of Commerce, clarifying the Chinese Kuomintang's accusation of the Chens General Consul of thirteen. The clarification was sent to Wu Kewei, on behalf of Wei, the ambassador to Peru, who was requested to transfer it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government. The original document rebutted each of the accusations. The seventh rebuttal stated: "Original text (Honorary Consul is called Consul General in Ecuador)". Chen, was appointed by the former Minister of Foreign Affairs, Yan Huiqing, of our government on July 27, 1922. It was approved by the Ecuadorian government on May 8, 1924. When the current President of Ecuador took office, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of our National Government telegraphed Consul General Chen, instructing him to represent the National Government as a Chinese Consul and offer congratulations. This is clear evidence that the National Government recognizes Chen as the Chinese Consul in Ecuador.

French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Strike, Report Yesterday 148

Public Security Bureau Calls Union for Talks

Trackless Trolley Attacked Again Yesterday

The French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Union, in view of the repeated damage to the company's water pipes and the dispatch of armed police to protect the company's repairs by the Public Security Bureau, sent Standing Committee Member Xu Amai to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday to report, stating briefly: "The workers have been on strike for a month. Twice...

###

Page 14

...the Bureau has called labor and management for mediation, but the French businessman has refused to listen and has repeatedly been absent. Their attitude of contempt for Chinese officials is extremely obvious. Regarding the damage to the water pipes, it was discovered that the Public Security Bureau sent police to protect the repairs. It should be known that this measure is beneficial to citizens and maintains the water supply, but the cause of this damage is that the factory has cut off the workers' livelihood and forced them to strike. They recruited new workers who were unfamiliar with the repairs, which is their own fault. Chinese officials are so protecting French businessmen that the lives of our 700 workers will be in a desperate situation. When can the victory of the strike be expected? Please help us." Guo Yongxi of the Third Section received them, accommodated their opinions, and agreed to discuss the matter with Section Chief Zhang.

More than 200 workers from the union went to the Municipal Party Department yesterday morning to petition and state their case. Comrade Yang of the Civil Training Committee received the representatives, Xu Amai and others, and agreed to forward it to the various committees and promised to find a way to help.

The union convened a meeting of all workers at 3:00 PM to discuss the matter. Xu Amai, the chairman, reported on the petition to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Department, stating briefly that the party, government, and military held a meeting and had specific measures for the labor unrest. "All the circumstances have been reported the day before yesterday. However, the victory of our strike depends on the assistance of the higher authorities, and also requires the assistance of all sectors. At the same time, it requires all workers to unite and struggle to achieve the goal of victory."

The union, during the strike period, was deeply afraid that a few workers would be incited by others and cause disturbances, which would not only hinder the strike but also be criticized. Therefore, it issued a notice to the workers to take special precautions and step up security to prevent reactionary elements from taking the opportunity to act. At 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon, Cui, a representative of Hua Dong Du, a director of the French Concession, came to the union, saying that Du asked to send representatives to come. Wang Agan, Zhang Amao, Zhang Qixiang, and Chen Puwen were sent. Du reported that the four workers who were released on bail by the French police were now required by the police to return to the case for investigation. He asked the two representatives to go to the union and ask the four previously detained people to come immediately. Chen Pu'ai and Zhang Qixiang returned to the union to report, and the masses were extremely grieved. After discussion, it was decided that of the four workers, two were released and two were released by Du. The two released by Du were Liu Linsheng and Zhou Aliuli. The original people volunteered to go to be detained on the spot. The two representatives accompanied them to Du's residence. Then Du sent someone to send the workers to the French police, but the police returned the original people to Du's house shortly after.

Yuan Liang, Director of the Public Security Bureau, fearing that reactionary elements would take the opportunity to mix in and incite the workers today and tomorrow, specially instructed Gao, the patrol officer of the Second District, to go to the union and call several representatives to talk yesterday. The union sent Zheng Ruisheng and Li Chuanqing to go. Director Yuan instructed that he hoped that all workers would take a calm attitude and not be incited by reactionary elements taking the opportunity to mix in, resulting in accidents. Then he explained the reason for protecting the company to repair the water pipes this time, hoping that the union would not misunderstand. The two representatives returned to the union and reported to the masses, all of whom complied.

At 11:25 yesterday noon, a French merchant's eighteenth Route No. 165 trackless trolley passing through the intersection of Xujiahui Road and Caishi Road was attacked by someone who threw a stone, damaging nine pieces of glass but not injuring anyone. By the time the French police arrived, the people had dispersed.

Labour unrest breaks out in Ewo Yarn Factory 149

According to Wen Wei Pao, the old Ewo Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road has stopped night work since last week due to the poor yarn market. It is stipulated that the original two shifts of day and night workers will take turns working every week. However, at about 5:00 yesterday morning (14th), when 1,500 workers who originally worked the night shift arrived at the factory to go to work, 150 workers who originally worked the day shift came forward to stop them, demanding a work stoppage protest, to prompt the factory to agree to the workers' demand that all 3,000 workers actually work five full days a week. After consultation between the factory manager and the workers' representatives, it was still unresolved at 11:30 in the morning, becoming a stalemate. The workers then left the factory together, and the factory was temporarily suspended. After the workers left the factory, about 100 people went east along Yangshupu Road, wanting to go to the new Ewo Factory on Weituoma Road. On the way, they arbitrarily picked up stones and threw them at several cars and one trolley car and four buses, breaking some car window glass. When they arrived in front of the new Yangshupu factory, they were blocked by Westerners inside the factory, and they took stones to throw at each other again. The patrolmen arrived and they dispersed.

Telephone Users Association Elects Directors 150

And Soliciting User Opinions

The Chinese Users Union of the China Foreign Telephone Company sent a letter to each user yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir/Madam, the telegram and telephone business of our country is clearly stipulated to be state-owned. However, this time, the International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation purchased the property of the China Foreign Telephone Company without the approval of our government and disregarded our national sovereignty. Although the government has repeatedly protested and the public has opposed it, the company has ignored it and is aggressively proceeding. Moreover, the company is purely for profit. Statistics show that the net profit of the business is as high as 100%, so the increase in telephone usage fees in the future will be endless, and the losses of users will inevitably be inevitable. The Ministry of Communications of the National Government of our country previously planned to recover and operate the China Foreign Telephone Company on its own due to its poor management. For the old Chinese shares, it is planned to exchange cash or convert them into new stocks at market prices after recovery, as commercial shares. For the old foreign shares, the Chinese businessmen will be allowed to recover them, or the government will buy them. For the future business prices, the prosperity of the business and the interests of the commercial shares are purely intended, which is incomparable to the mere profit-seeking of foreign businessmen. All users of China Foreign Telephone Company have suffered from the bad influence of past telephones, of course, they believe that unless the telephone business is completely recovered by the government and directly supervised by our government, it is not enough to protect national rights and seek improvement. In order to support national sovereignty and maintain the interests of users, our association has organized the Chinese Users Union of China Foreign Telephone Company. All Chinese users are members. The association is located on the third floor of Shanghai Hong Kong No. 4 and started working on July 1st to actively promote and support the government. We hope that all Chinese users will work together to advocate the purpose of supporting national rights and maintaining interests. Therefore, we have attached a copy of the association's articles of association and sent it to you, hoping that you will check and fully express your opinions, and indicate the strategy to proceed. Because the time was urgent, our association was hurriedly organized and established, and Li Zuchong, Hua Huizhong, Zhu Yinjiang, Tao Ledong, Hu Fengxiang, Wang Zhiwei, Cheng Zhusun, Jin Runxiang, Zhang Yichen, and nine others were appointed as temporary directors to take charge of the association's affairs. We should nominate and elect formally in accordance with the regulations to achieve soundness. For this reason, we also ask you to nominate three candidates for directors from among the users you know and send them to our association within three days, so that we can decide on a plan and formally elect them. Sincerely, The Chinese Users Union of China Foreign Telephone Company."

The One Who Lends at High Interest Dies! 152

Jin Yuanlin Dies Suddenly from Acute Disease

Jin Yuanlin from Zhejiang (nickname "Little Huzhou"), who lived at a certain address on North Henan Road in the Public Concession and specialized in lending at high interest, was 37 years old. Yesterday afternoon around 6 o'clock, while holding his one or two-year-old son, he went to Chen Xiji's house at No. 4 Deshan Lane on Rue du Consulat in the French Concession to collect interest. After entering the door with the child in his arms, his face suddenly turned pale, and his body was covered in cold sweat like beads. In less than five minutes, without saying a word, he died suddenly from an acute illness. The Chen family, seeing this situation, was stunned. Later, they sent someone to notify the deceased's concubine, known as Xiao Laosi, to come. Suspecting foul play, they reported the incident to the Louza Police Station. After the head detective sent an investigator to examine the scene, it was determined that he had died from an acute illness. The head detective allowed the woman to claim the body for burial. As a result, the woman borrowed a coffin from a charity organization and hastily buried the deceased, temporarily placing him in the Huzhou Guild Hall in Zhabei, it is said.

A Victim of Flower Gambling 153

Yang Linshi's Tragic Last Words

Yang Haiting from Anhui has been running the Yangchun Beef Noodle Restaurant at No. 359 Lane on South City Road, Guan Bridge. He had a son named Jin Biao, who was 41 years old and ran a beef stall near the restaurant. The year before last, through a matchmaker, he married a woman from Ningbo named Linshi. She was 36 years old. After the marriage, the couple's relationship was relatively harmonious. Jin Biao gave all his earnings to her for safekeeping. However, she was addicted to flower gambling and would often bet tens of taels of silver at a time. After losing all her savings, she even pawned her clothes and jewelry to continue gambling. Unexpectedly, she lost every time. Recently, she gambled away all the money her husband gave her daily. Having run out of money, she was afraid of being scolded by her husband, so she hid the truth. Around 9 a.m. the day before yesterday, Jin Biao needed to pay the beef company, and asked her for money, but she didn't respond for a long time. Suspecting something, he questioned her, and she confessed the truth. Jin Biao was extremely angry and immediately scolded her. She was already heavily in debt and now faced her husband's condemnation. Feeling resentful, she secretly went into the room, swallowed opium behind everyone's back, and lay down on the bed. Around 2 p.m., the family discovered her, seeing her face pale. Suspecting she was ill, they urgently called her awake and rushed her to the Red Cross South City Hospital for treatment. After examination, the doctor realized she had taken poison. He quickly tried to save her, but it was too late, and the poison had already taken effect. She soon died. As she was dying, she tearfully said to her husband, "Because I was addicted to flower gambling, I lost all your money, clothes, and jewelry. I have failed you, and I cannot die in peace." After saying this, she passed away. Yang immediately reported the situation to the local District One Police Station and explained the facts of his wife Linshi's life. The district chief, considering it a matter of life and death, ordered Lu Yongde, the sixteenth ward head, to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an inquest. Yesterday afternoon around 4 p.m., Prosecutor Zhao, accompanied by the coroner, arrived at the scene and confirmed that Yang Linshi had indeed died from poisoning. He ordered the family to sign a guarantee and claim the body for burial. After the inquest, he returned to the court to report.

Two Boxes of Flower Gambling Slips 154

Why Did Gan Dushi Die?

Gan Dushi, a woman living at No. 3 South Chujia Bridge in the French Concession, had been widowed for several years. She had some savings and a son who was already of age, but he was not good at making a living and seemed to have a mental disorder. Gan Dushi also had a legal wife in her hometown, who also had a son who was married. However, they were far away from Shanghai and rarely visited. In Shanghai, she and her son were able to make ends meet. In recent years, she had become addicted to flower gambling, secretly betting and losing all her savings in the past year or two. She even pawned her clothes and jewelry, seeking divine guidance and hoping for a lucky bet. Unexpectedly, she lost again, resulting in extreme financial hardship. However, she never revealed her situation outwardly, while feeling extremely anxious inside. In the end, she died suddenly at the end of last month due to anxiety. She had no possessions left behind. The legal wife and son from her hometown came to Shanghai, intending to divide her inheritance. During the initial mourning period, because not all relatives were present, the boxes were not opened. It was not until the memorial ceremony that all the relatives gathered and opened the boxes. There were no complete clothes, only two boxes of flower gambling slips and scrap paper. As a result, the legal wife and son wanted to flee. The relatives ordered them to bear the funeral expenses, shouting that it was bad luck and a jinx.

Retrial Verdict in Apprentice Dies from Kicking Case 155

Six Months Imprisonment Overturned

Civil Portion Remains as Originally Judged

Hu Atong, a Shaoxing native who worked as a partner in the Wanhua Cheng Laundry opened by Zhang Binghao from Wenzhou on Rue de Sévigné in the French Concession, kicked his apprentice Liu Caidong in March of this year, causing injury. Liu Caidong died in the laundry on May 24. Afterwards, the deceased's mother Liu Meishi sued Hu in the French court for causing injury, requesting a trial and compensation for damages. After repeated interrogations, the court sentenced Hu to six months imprisonment and ordered him to pay the plaintiff 500 yuan in compensation. Hu, dissatisfied with the initial verdict, hired lawyer Gu Jirong to represent him and submitted a petition for retrial. The retrial was approved, and he was interrogated yesterday. Lawyer Gu argued on behalf of the appellant, and the plaintiff claimed that the initial court had not determined the cause of death of the deceased and rashly convicted the appellant. Although the appellant had a dispute with the deceased in March, he did not kick him in the chest, and the deceased continued to work as usual without any sign of injury until he died two months later. It was difficult to prove whether he died from the kick. Therefore, the original verdict should be overturned or the sentence reduced, and the appellant had previously agreed to pay some compensation. The laundry owner and others testified in court about the situation at the time. Judge Gong ruled to overturn the six-month imprisonment sentence of the initial verdict, stating that the civil portion of the initial verdict was reasonable and should be enforced as originally judged.

Gu Ayou Can't Forget the Widow 156

Two Thefts of Photographs

Involving Two University Students

The Third Branch of the Zhenru Fourth District Security Bureau reported the day before yesterday (the 12th) that Jinan University students Li Shaobai and Zhou Chuanfeng had reported that a thief, Gu Ayou, had stolen money and items from their flat at No. 16 Lijia Ge. The police were dispatched to arrest him and brought the victim Li Xueshi to the station. Acting Director Shi questioned the plaintiff Li Shaobai, who stated that he was from Sanyuan, Shaanxi. He and Zhou rented a room at Li Xueshi's house. This morning, they suddenly saw the defendant Gu Ayou hurriedly leaving their room with a paper package. They did not know him, but his suspicious behavior indicated that he must be a thief, so they reported it to the bureau for arrest. Zhou, from Jishui, Jiangxi, 24 years old, gave a similar statement. Gu Ayou, a 43-year-old farmer from Shanghai, confessed that he had always been a bachelor. Recently, Li Xueshi's mother insisted on marrying her daughter to him. He felt sorry for the widow and paid a dowry of 100 yuan, planning to marry her next month. However, Xueshi was frivolous and had been having an affair with the university student Zhou and others. Knowing that she had changed her mind and there would be no good outcome, he was still resentful. So, this morning, he sneaked into Xueshi's bedroom and stole a photo of her as a memento. Li Xueshi, from Wuxi, 33 years old, stated that Li Shaobai and others were her tenants. Her husband had died many years ago, and she made a living by working. Unexpectedly, Gu had been trying to seduce her to marry him. She refused, and he stole her photo and fled. Li and others reported it to the police, who arrested him. The director, based on the confession, suspected that Gu Ayou's theft of Xueshi's photo was motivated by other reasons. However, since the matter was trivial, he released Gu on bail. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning, Gu took the opportunity to sneak into Xueshi's room again and hid her photo in his pocket. When Li and others were about to go to school, they saw Gu stealing something again and handed him over to the police, who sent him to the bureau again. During the interrogation by the director, Gu Ayou became delusional, claiming that the university student had committed adultery with his wife, which was extremely shameless, and his words were incoherent. The director, considering that Gu had repeatedly stolen Xueshi's photo and there might be other issues involved, immediately prepared a document to send Gu, Xueshi, Li Shaobai, and Zhou Chuanfeng together to the Judicial Section for review.

Chinese National Weekly, Issue 5 Published 165

The English Chinese National Weekly has been well received by readers since its publication, and its circulation has been increasing daily. Issue 5 has been published today, and the content is even richer. This issue features a special article by RANDALL GOULD, "What Foreign Correspondents Found on the Front," which is particularly brilliant. It describes the front-line situation as seen by the reporters, with a fair and accurate account. It is essential reading for those who care about the current situation. Other highlights include the legality of Simpson's seizure of the Tianjin Customs and the sale of telephone issues in the Shanghai Public Concession. The publishing department is located on the fourth floor of the Western Building, No. 1 Jiujiang Road, and major bookstores are selling it.

The Shanghai Women's Hairdressing School, located at No. 200 Ximen Road, held its 16th graduation ceremony the day before yesterday. Pan Yuying, Li Yunxiang, Chen Yunqing, and Peng Yunqiu have gone to Yunnan Anqing to prepare for the establishment of women's hairdressing salons. The Jiangsu Second District Baijiu and Taijiabao Tobacco and Alcohol Public Sale Fee Collection Office has received provincial orders to continue handling the 19th-year tax fees. Chinese Philosophical Society Invents Strengthening Technique 168

Mr. Lin Zihe, president of the Chinese Philosophical Society at No. 22 Mingde Lane, Avenue Joffre, has invented a strengthening technique that can be taught to all sectors at any time. It is completely taught using physical education methods. Therefore, those who obtain this technique can not only prolong their lives but also maintain good health forever. It is said that Mr. Lin, in order to offer preferential treatment to those who inquire, exempts all fees except for the membership fee. Those who wish to obtain detailed information can send a letter with a four-cent stamp attached, and it will be mailed immediately.

Timber Ship Runs Aground in Hurricane 169

The Wen-Tai-helping sand ship Baoxing, which was loading a large batch of timber from Fuzhou to Shanghai for unloading, arrived at the mouth of the Songjiang River around 7 p.m. the night before last. It was already dark, and a hurricane was raging with rough waves. The ship lost control and drifted with the wind and waves. It drifted to the Shizilin waters outside Wusongkou and ran aground on a beach. The ship immediately broke apart, and all the timber on board was scattered. The crew members all fell into the water. Fortunately, neighboring fishing boats risked their lives to rescue the crew one by one. Yesterday morning, the shipowner Chen Luji landed at Shizilin, walked to Songjiang, and hired a boat to go to the scene to try to salvage the timber. However, most of the timber had drifted away. The estimated loss is about 30,000 yuan.

Western Pigment Industry: Since its establishment, the Shanghai Western Pigment Industry Association has been handling member negotiation cases and mediating settlements on a daily basis, which have become increasingly complex. Currently, the association's standing committee members Zhang Rulin, Ma Shangjie, and Zhang Jinshou have returned to their hometowns for various reasons. Recently, the association's affairs have been handled by standing committee member Xi Rungeng, who attends meetings to review cases and supervise staff, actively working with great enthusiasm and treating the staff with unusual kindness and consideration. Currently, the work is focused on the document section, and the person in charge of handling documents, Wei Shidiao, works diligently all day long, even in the sweltering heat of the electric fan. At present, the focus is on the active and important work of handling the case of some colleagues in the illegal organization who refuse to join the association. Most of these colleagues are those who earned the most profit in the pigment business during the European War. Their attitude is capitalistic, stubborn, and unreasonable. The association adheres to the spirit of the party, bears the mission of the party, and further plans to express the spirit of the law under the party's rule, restriction, and prohibition.

Da Baozi Dies by Drowning 171

Wang Dabaozi, from Yancheng, 14 years old, was a worker in the Fuxin Flour Factory No. 2 in the Tanziwan area of Zhabei. Yesterday afternoon around 5 p.m., Wang left work and intended to take the nearby ferry home. However, the passengers were unusually crowded at the time. Wang, being young and weak, was pushed and lost his footing, falling into the canal. Although people tried to rescue him, they were unable to recover him. Someone notified his father, Wang Yigan, who reported the incident to the Fourth District Headquarters. The ferryman Wan Changyun was detained by the headquarters. After a brief questioning of both sides, the case was related to a human life, and a document was prepared to transfer the case to the General Bureau for review.

News from Various Labor Unions 172

Four Labor Unions Including the South Goods Workers' Union: The South Goods Workers' Union, the Yangna Industry Workers' Union, the South District Factory Workers' Union, and the Taikang Food Company Workers' Union oppose the International Company's purchase of the Sino-Foreign Telephone Company. The statement says the telephone company is a large enterprise in the international development plan and has a close relationship with the national economy and the people's livelihood. Now, imperialism, using economic power in the name of an international company, has contracted to purchase the full rights of the Sino-Foreign Telephone Company in the concession. This is a clear further suppression of our people's livelihood with the power of capital. In the past, imperialism has used all possible strategies to invade our country. This time, the International Company, without the permission of our government, privately transferred and dared to buy all the property rights of the Sino-Foreign Telephone Company, which is a blatant contempt for our country's sovereignty. Now, although our Ministry of Foreign Affairs has argued with reason, the unreasonable imperialism still continues to sign the agreement as if it did not hear anything. If it is realized, then the suffering Chinese will be more oppressed by imperialism. Compatriots across the country, to maintain the life of the country, we must oppose the International Company's purchase of the Sino-Foreign Telephone Company's property rights in the Shanghai Concession. We must unite and support our country's diplomacy. The Sino-Foreign Telephone Company should be nationalized.

Silk and Cloth Dyeing Workers' Union: In view of the business failures of the capitalists and the increasing number of unemployed members, the executive committee decided to conduct a general registration of unemployed members. It started yesterday, the 15th. The deadline for Shanghai is one week, and the deadline for other places is two weeks. All silk and cloth workers who hold the union's membership card can register within the specified period, every day from 7 a.m. to 11 a.m. The union reported to the Municipal Training Association that a city-wide representatives' conference will be held tomorrow (the 17th) at 7 p.m. to discuss the unemployment problem and request assistance from the higher authorities.

(1) Regarding the loss of silk in Chunhua, it was resolved that the organization department is responsible for handling it. (3, 4, 5, 6) All omitted. (9) Regarding the organization of small groups and branch secretaries, it was resolved that the propaganda department should organize two groups and actively proceed. (10) Regarding the establishment of a clinic, it was resolved to retain it. (11) Omitted. (12) Regarding the member Yu Zishan's voluntary work in the union, it was resolved to appoint Yu Zishan as a voluntary secretary. (13) Omitted. (24) Regarding the case of Wu Changren and Bai Yongchang's long-term absence from the union and neglecting their work, it was resolved to recommend Gu Aibao to temporarily serve as propaganda and Dai Jianyun to temporarily serve as training, and report to the Civil Training Association for record. Weather Report 173

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday said that the Yangtze River basin and the coast south of Ma'an Island are mostly cloudy with southeast winds. There is a strong cyclone in the Shandong and Liaodong Peninsulas. Because the hurricane is moving north or northeast, it will pass through the area. There is another hurricane in the Pacific Ocean that has entered the east of Luzon and will move northwestward. Also, within 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 87.8 and the lowest was 74.8. On the same day last year, the highest was 96.1 and the lowest was 76.0.

Art World 174

Peasant Art 175

By Yamamoto Kenzo

Translated by Chen Baoyi

(2)

Industrial peasant art, though currently practiced in various parts of Europe, I have not examined its actual state in detail. Based on fragmented observations, it seems to be declining in highly industrialized areas like England. Originally, places like England are not known for peasant art, and the countryside seems to be on the verge of desolation. According to Mr. Buhira of the Agricultural Policy Section of the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, there is a recent movement in England to revive rural crafts.

It is said that Lloyd George once stated, "Farmers have recently been drawn to rural home industries. For example, in the rural areas of Wales, methods of toy making are being taught, focusing on rural areas." The planned revival includes the production of wooden toys, wood carvings, tinplate handicrafts, leather handicrafts, basket making, lace, hand-woven fabrics, etc.

In Germany, which strives to promote small industries and focuses on managing "so-called dispersed labor," and in Russia, which has a large number of farmers and confines outdoor labor to the dreadfully long and cold winters, this kind of peasant art seems to be thriving. In Germany, various craft vocational schools are established to educate the children of farmers. For independent producers, there are craft conference centers jointly run by the government and private sectors in cities large and small nationwide. These seem to be organizations specifically designed to promote the formation of groups and aid the development of isolated craftspeople. Rural crafts, in particular, have the support of powerful sponsoring organizations. In large cities, they set up sales outlets, hold exhibitions, and give lectures, striving to promote and encourage them. In Russia and Italy, when promoting peasant art, the practice seems to be to draw inspiration from the ancient arts of their own countries. However, Germany is different. In German craft schools, the emphasis is generally on encouraging originality. For example, the motto of the renowned rural school in Wunhamroit, which teaches processing of white cloth, is "Simple, Strong, Bold." The aforementioned sponsoring organizations aimed at supporting craftspeople declare to the producers, "We hope that people themselves can discover their own originality, creative ability, and past successes and future possibilities. For all artisans who work in accordance with our principles, we will provide practical efforts and promote their businesses."

Russian peasant handicrafts, in terms of the large number of practitioners, can probably be considered the best in the world. In a report by the Russian Agricultural Administration about seventeen years ago, it was written, "Russian peasant handicrafts, although composed of vaguely defined small units, are an important production value second only to agricultural products." It also stated, "Russian peasant handicrafts include all categories of occupational industries."

From this, one can roughly get a glimpse of its widespread expansion. Since becoming Labor-Peasant Russia, peasant art seems to have been imagined as falling into decline, but there are also those who say that it is even more prosperous than in the imperial era. Regardless of which is true, the fact remains that the Labor-Peasant government values peasant handicrafts. The evidence for this can be seen in the fact that peasant handicrafts are directly under the Supreme Economic Council of Soviet Russia, with important figures as its leaders, and a specialized weekly newspaper is published.

In Russia, besides peasant art for self-use and industrial purposes, there is also a type of peasant art that can be called culturalism or an art movement – famous peasant art. This is the handicrafts centered on the Talashkino workshop led by Princess Maria Tenisheva, which was expanded to the ancient rural villages of Smolensk. Princess Tenisheva's ideas for this project seem to resonate with William Morris of England (Note B). Princess Maria shared Morris's hopes for the city and focused on the rural people.

That is, she wanted to enrich the daily lives of rural villagers with fine art, crafts, music, and theater, and to elevate their emotions. At that time, the princess and seven artists took rural men and women as disciples, and what they taught them was probably not only the techniques of dyeing, embroidery, or woodworking, wood carving, etc., but also deeper artistic intelligence. In short, the princess paid special attention to the fabric crafts called "Smolensk Embroidery," which had a modern flavor, were simple, and had an elegant quality. However, what has become of that lineage that originated only twenty years ago?

(Note B: William Morris was an English designer, poet, and socialist who established factories to promote fine art and crafts.)

To be suitable for the true meaning of folk education, and on one hand, to reflect urban tastes without falling into competition with mechanical products, but rather to coexist and oppose it, is necessary – where should the goal of future peasant art be placed? – I look back on my own experiences and have received many suggestions from the Smolensk fabric crafts. I see that the absence or complete demise of crafts for self-use and the lack of vitality in industrial peasant art produced in modern rural areas are inevitable. However, the techniques honed by industrial use may at some point be applied to produce living peasant art.

Thoughts After Viewing the Bai E Painting Exhibition by Guan Han 176

What is the difference between thoughts and criticism? Thoughts are subjective, while criticism is objective. However, whether subjective or objective, all conclusions must be based on something. To state my reason for writing these thoughts, I cannot avoid starting with a familiar opening.

I am ashamed to say that I am simply not qualified to judge other people's art. Although I am a follower in the art world, I have never received profound artistic knowledge. The genesis of these thoughts can be said to be from my own understanding, and I have some grasp of it. Even though I have not fully learned in the art garden, I have not stopped studying. Therefore, all the art exhibitions at sea leave my footprints.

This time, the Bai E Research Institute's practice exhibition gave me a deep impression. Although there were not many exhibits, it has given me many new paths. Each painting has its own characteristics. The ones I admire and respect the most are:

(1) Fang Xuegu's "Flower-like Temptation," depicting a bare-shouldered girl with her eyes gazing sideways, a white flower hanging on her shoulder. The meaning is profound, and the colors are good. Speaking of the expression, it is no different from reality. Anyone who sees it will be fascinated, and it is indeed a "flower-like temptation."

(2) Pan Sitong's "Evening Anchorage" is extremely majestic. The coloring is very exquisite, depicting countless returning boats gathered on the river, with the setting sun shining obliquely, red light and green water, reflecting each other, making it even more magnificent.

(3) Luo Tianmin's "Fair Wind" depicts the image vividly. Looking back, the sailing boatman seems to be moving forward with the wind. The beauty of this lies in the slightly inclined front mast, as if pressed by the wind, while the rear mast stands upright and unyielding. Because the rear mast is the main object and much stronger than the front mast, it does not succumb to the wind. This is logically correct and is also Luo's unique point.

(4) Chen Qiucao's "Hazy Night" best expresses the transparency of matter, while using very simple colors. The depicted twilight scene is extraordinarily desolate. In the shady jungle by the roadside, hangs a dim and dying moon. On the desolate road, a traveler is busy hurrying home. The light of the lantern he holds is pale and bleak. This kind of quiet and desolate situation is written extremely thoroughly even in a small-sized painting. It is truly a skillful hand.

The above-mentioned paintings are indeed top-notch. I love them most, but there are many other fine works, such as Zhou Xi's "Lamplight," Xuegu's "Desolate Street," and the works of Qiu Hen, Zhi Zhen, and Xue Ou. Each has its own characteristics and is very wonderful. There are also

"Wilderness," two paintings, He Aizhen's is better because the river surface is vast, and a small piece of paper can accommodate unlimited scenery. It is not only spectacular, but also allows the viewer's heart to be broadened with the line of sight. Aizhen's painting is superior in this regard. Looking at the Bai E exhibition as a whole, the results are not bad. It really does not disappoint my time and expectations.

Everyone knows that the backward Chinese art world is difficult to progress. However, in recent years, the promotion of painting has been extremely enthusiastic, and the number of art gardens responsible for guidance has also increased. On the surface, it seems to be a good phenomenon in the Chinese art world, but few authors of true spirit have been produced, and great works are rarely seen. This is probably because the scholars in the art gardens do not value the value of art. Perhaps because the graduation time in the art gardens is predetermined, scholars do not get enough basic research time, so it is difficult to make the appreciators sympathize with the works. There are also many erroneous atoms. I don't want to go into detail anymore, because the content of this article is only to express feelings for Bai E, so writing to this point will be temporarily considered an ending. I will write another article for discussion when I have the opportunity.

The Story of World Literature (179) by John Macy, Translated by Hu Zhongchi 177

Chapter 46: Scandinavian Literature

Hawthorne entered the scene honestly with his deep interest in people's souls. This was because he was a descendant of the Puritans of New England. Although he himself was not a Puritan, he contemplated matters of conscience just like his ancestors. However, he studied the conflicts of character with the intention of constructing stories from them. He contemplated as an artist in general, whereas the New Englanders of the past were not artists at all. They were serious, uninteresting people without much awareness of beauty, and they actually believed that beautiful things must be evil. Hawthorne turned them around and made them interesting.

His father and grandfather were ship captains of Salem, Massachusetts,

that once-thriving commercial port. He may have gone to sea and written nautical romances, but he stopped on land instead of sailing on the ship of literature. As his friend Ralph Waldo Emerson said of him, he rode the horse of hermitage and rode it well. After graduating from Bowdoin College, he lived in solitude, writing short stories and honing his writing style, which was excellent. Some of the short stories are small masterpieces. However, for a long time, the American public did not give his works a sincere welcome. Only a few writers, including Edgar Allan Poe, appreciated his value. Hawthorne himself even claimed to be the most humble of American writers.

(1) The text is limited to news, reviews, and introductions about recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

Book Review

Modern Writer by Wen Zhi 179

By Wang Fen

Published by Zhen Mei Shan

"Modern Writer" includes ten short stories: "Behind the Mountain," "Escape," "Two Rows," "An Old Man," "Temptation," "Modern Writer," "Fourth Night of the New Year," "In the Accumulation of Snow," "In Front of the Rainy Mountain," "Visiting the Grave." Each of these stories has a different type of person. In these different types of people, the author expresses them very delicately. Indeed, in this era, these characters can be found no matter what. In our daily lives, these characters can also be seen. However, in the eyes of ordinary people, they are often easily overlooked. The author, however, firmly grasps them, without letting go of a single detail. For example, "An Old Man," if we go out, old men like this are easily seen. "A train flashed past the window. As soon as the train moved, the old man leaned back and cursed the train, the driver, and even the current road administration. However, he also spoke of important party and state officials, and those who heard it turned pale." (Page 34) The Chinese are most fond of cursing others, but they are not aware of themselves, so that they end up "not being able to say it clearly." Moreover, they are accustomed to pleasing themselves, being selfish, and blaming others for being selfish. Knowing the contradiction, they are still unwilling to admit defeat. Secondly, they like to talk nonsense, flatter those above them, and oppress those below them. The old man even said, "I had expected that you two are students. So well-behaved. Really. The current situation is only possible with students. Good for them to study. Studying to do things for the public. So patriotic. If they didn't parade and give speeches, we probably wouldn't know about national shame and National Day. Ah, students always see things clearly." (Page 36) This may be the ancient style of respecting scholars, because "As soon as the car stopped, the old man let the students who were crowding at the door go first, and then he rushed to leave first." So, what kind of impression does this old man who emerges in our minds leave?

Originally, the subject matter of creation does not need to be so far-fetched. Selecting fragments of life from the ranks of the people and expressing them with artistic skill is indeed needed at this time. Because the author is influenced by rural life, his descriptions tend to focus on rural areas and the lower classes. He does not like to pursue trends, so he does not like to depict youthful romances.

The ten works in "Modern Writer" all have distinct styles. The author's descriptive skills are very economical. Like the rascal who opened the coffin to steal the corpse's clothes, I have heard this story since I was a child. Now the author focuses on the psychological description, which vividly jumps on the paper. This increases the infinite horror more than hearing it. Also, like the matter of opium prohibition, the ugly history of "those in their positions seeking their own interests" has been seen countless times. It is true that "to be honest," how can opium be completely prohibited? Now, aren't we both breaking the law here?" Then, corrupt officials will never be completely overthrown. Also, like the author describing the little-footed aunt's widowhood and loss of virtue, this symbolizes the danger of modern women. Once tempted, they change their minds. "The breasts are as high as when she came, only the belly is a little different." Also, like Bai Gengyu rushing to gamble, but being caught by the gamblers, because his braid was grabbed, he became angry and "tonight is all because of this braid" took scissors and cut it off. The description is very profound.

The author's description of children's innocence is both cute, funny, and pitiful. "San Gou was very happy, because tomorrow's dish will be eaten by himself after all. He knew that Grandpa would not eat it. In his mind, meat, braised pork, vegetables with pork, braised until red, with a lot of sugar, the soup is purple, that's how it tastes. Fish is fish braised with greens, with small bones, hard, not tasty. Shredded pork, shredded pork is also good. Golden flower vegetables, he won't touch them tomorrow. Thinking, his throat gurgled, and he swallowed a mouthful of saliva." (Page 134) Not saying that putting the kite on top of people's houses means losing a sumptuous grave-visiting meal.

The author is a student, so naturally he is inevitably touched by school life. "This collection is named 'Modern Writer' because what is described in this article is a way of life that I have never observed in my past eighteen years, and the encounter with this matter has made the deepest impression on my heart." (Page 5) It can be seen that the author's impression is profound, so the writing is particularly energetic. This describes the arrogance of a college student publishing a new literary book. Later, the members found out that the cover was something from the club, so they questioned him. As a result, he withdrew and started the Spring Breeze Society three days later. Characters like Mr. Ping are everywhere among modern college students. In fact, they just don't have the cultivation of group life, only know how to be selfish. In this collection, the author's satirical tone is very strong. Precisely because of this, it is more powerfully set off.

I like "In Front of the Rainy Mountain" and "Visiting the Grave" the most. The structure and the like are better than the other chapters. Secondly, "Modern Writer" and "Behind the Mountain." However, it seems that the author has a kind of shortcoming in the collection, that is, the atmosphere of depression, distress, pessimism, and sadness is too strong. Although I am not absolutely demanding a generous spirit and an exciting tone, I always think that we should inject energetic, hopeful, bright, willful, and spiritual blood serum into society, with considerable enlightenment. We can't sting like a poisonous bee's sting that is irrelevant. We have found the crux, and we have to overcome it. Then the author is a "warrior." Let's wait for the publication of the second collection.

Women's Reading Afterthoughts 180

A collection of short stories by Ling Shuhua

Like a sparrow's nimble thoughts, a snake's agile penmanship, this is the most fitting description of Ms. Shuhua. Although her thoughts are not particularly expansive, encompassing all of life, she can still use her vividly depicted women to give readers a deep impression through her criticisms of servants, the lives of female students, and everything else.

We all know the author is a "woman," so she can especially deeply depict the psychology of women. Although some may say she exaggerates too much, I believe this is possible. Don't you believe in the Yu Ru in "Sickness"? This kind of person exists. If you still don't believe me now, then I can briefly record Yu Ru's deeds so everyone can see:

Yu Ru's husband, Zhiqing, was sick. She advised him to go to Xishan to recuperate, but because they had no money, they couldn't go. Yu Ru couldn't bear to see her beloved husband continue like this, not getting treatment, so she borrowed money everywhere, but all her efforts were in vain. While cursing the coldness of the world, she started painting and selling her paintings to earn money and go to recuperate with her beloved husband. While painting, she suffered her beloved husband's suspicion, and her husband even considered divorce. Later, everyone finally understood.

Here, I can say that the woman is worthy of praise, and such women are possible in the world. As for the man, Zhiqing's suspicion is just a common kind of jealousy. I say that the characters in this novel are very ordinary, but what is valuable is that the author can describe things so wonderfully, without making people feel that this is an ordinary thing.

The above is regarding the technique and structure of the "Sickness" piece. As for its content, it is a major social issue.

People should work, but because of "sickness," should they rest? If they should rest, but have no money, how should they solve this problem? This becomes a social problem. As for Yu Ru forging other people's paintings, using deceitful means to trick people, there is inevitably a moral flaw. Although Zhiqing reproached her, she said:

"I don't care anymore, I can't control it anymore," such heartbreaking words. From the perspective of "emotion," it is "understandable," but from the perspective of reason, it is immoral. Can we accept such people in the world? This becomes a very difficult problem to solve.

Indeed, this is just one example in Ms. Shuhua's works. Many others also have this characteristic: placing the contradictions and shortcomings of society in the work. If we analyze and introduce this collection carefully, we can gain even more.

In the article "Little Liu," Little Liu used to ridicule women with children. When Little Liu was a student, there was a woman in her class, so she gathered her comrades and wanted to report her to the principal, not allowing the woman to study. Later, she thought it would be better to directly ridicule the woman, so during sewing class, she arbitrarily joked about the woman, and as a result, the woman ran away. During this joking, the author vividly portrays that playful attitude of Little Liu and her party, with a pen as agile as a snake emerging from its hole.

After Little Liu went through this student era,

she finally had children herself. Such a contradictory fact, and the marriage of those who advocate celibacy, are commonly seen among young people. I said that the author is accustomed to writing about ordinary things, but the writing is extraordinary, that is "good."

The "Mr. Li" piece is a bit lesser. The main theme is not obvious, but the calm attitude of the protagonist, Mr. Li, can still give the reader some impression. As for what she said when she was a dean,

"Every Sunday," most of the letters are love letters, "It's no wonder, these children are at the age of writing love letters,"...

She lightly and clearly impresses the common things in school life on the paper and runs into the reader's mind.

Yes, these are common things in schools.

The theme of "Seeing off the Car" is a humorous matter (that is, the author often likes to use humorous facts in other articles), but in the dark, it fully praises a woman who specializes in criticizing the shortcomings of servants, for example:

"Miss Wang, you haven't managed a household, so you don't know the shortcomings of the people below. Alas, there isn't a single honest one. The other day I asked him to buy a chicken, and when I weighed it, it was clearly a little over one catty and four ounces,

but he reported one catty and five ounces. Bean sprouts are fourteen coppers a catty, I asked a few days ago, and he said people won't sell it for less than fifteen coppers..."

The whole article is full of such talk about the shortcomings of servants. No wonder her husband had to stop her and say:

"Why don't you change the subject? Always talking about them, aren't you tired of it?"

Yes, it's too much, just like young students who love to talk about the opposite sex, they themselves don't feel tired of it.

Enough small talk, I will say one more "Woman" and then shut up.

The layout of "Woman" is so lovable, humorous and tight, everywhere showing the author's painstaking tailoring, and even more showing the author's innocence. The Second Honest in the whole "Woman" article is very noticeable and lovable. Let's optimistically wait for the future masters of China. The female protagonist's gentle means separate the two of them. I say it's both interesting and very effective. Isn't this article a proof, friends? If you encounter such a thing, please try it like this.

This article is also very well written and very satisfying. Shuhua used it as the book title for this reason.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 181

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction. However, trivial books will not be introduced.

(2) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(3) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

Mr. Guo Gu Ni's Paintings 182

(4) Each text should not exceed 3,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and do not be sloppy with the words. Western texts can be omitted as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures attached to the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. You must use white paper and black drawings.

(8) Please specify "Book and Newspaper Introduction Department" for incoming manuscripts.

(9) Incoming manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. If you need to return them, you should declare in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) The remuneration for texts is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. The remuneration for pictures and photos is also the same as this example. For special manuscripts, the remuneration will be calculated separately.
